[2026-01-10T08:10:54Z] Ryan Colaço: What a great theme and set @⁨~Pavan Pamidimarri⁩ ↵ 'Guns, germs, and steel' has a great related point on why, although PNG started off at the same situation as some Polynesian countries... It continues to be so linguistically diverse... (Asked gpt to help me frame the following, because I was struggling to articulate it well): ↵  _An intriguing part at the beginning of Jared Diamond’s Guns, Germs, and Steel highlights the contrast between Papua New Guinea, Indonesia, and the Polynesian countries (Hawaii, Samoa, etc). All of these regions began with similar conditions: numerous indigenous languages, small-scale societies, and long geographic separation from other advanced civilizations._ ↵ _Yet their historical trajectories diverged dramatically. In Polynesia, the development of extraordinarily effective seafaring* enabled long-distance settlement, sustained inter-island contact, and the spread of a relatively unified language and culture across vast oceanic distances. By contrast, Papua New Guinea and much of Indonesia remained highly fragmented. Their rugged mountains, dense forests, and scattered islands limited both movement and large-scale integration. This fragmentation was compounded by their *north–south orientation* , which spans sharply different climates and ecological zones over short distances, making the transfer of crops, animals, and technological innovations extremely difficult. Polynesia, by contrast, benefited from more consistent climates along the islands they colonized, and their seafaring networks reinforced integration rather than isolation. Diamond’s comparison illustrates how geography, climate orientation, and technological innovation together shape patterns of settlement, societal structure, and the astonishing diversity of human languages and cultures._ ↵ *interestingly, many centuries before Europeans achieved intercontinental travel... Had to bring this up to get a Portuguese colleague to pipe down when he was being pompous about how they first managed to crack long-distance travel by sea
